ARIE 1921-1922 [vol. 044]


A.--List of copper plates examined during the year 1921-22.


ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/1 (page 9)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Pendyala Venkata-subrahmanya Sastri, National College, Bandar, through the Tahsildar of Bandar, Kistna district.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 940 (in words), Jyē-shṭa, Kṛish-ṇa-paksha, navamī, Sun-day.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the Tahsildar of Bandar.
Edition
…
Remarks
Records the grant of the village [Tā]ḍipāḍi as an agrahāra and two tanks by the Malaya chiefs Kāma-rāju Eṟama-rāju, Immaḍi Beḍaṅga-rāju, Śōḍapa-rāju, Kaliyuga Kaṇ-ṇa-rāju and Mārvala Garuḍa to Naḍupa-Nāyaka the general of Chōḍaya-rāja. The record is written very indifferently.
ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/2 (page 9)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Pendyala Venkata-subrahmanya Sastri, National College, Bandar, through the President, District Board, Godavari district.
Dynasty
Eastern Chāḷukya
King
Indravarma-Mahārāja alias Tyāgadhēnu.
Date
…
Language
Sanskrit in archaic Telugu characters
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Gift of the village Koṇḍanāgūru by the king as a brahmadēya to the brahman Cheṇḍi-śarman of the Bhāradvāja-gōtra and the Vājasanēya-charaṇa. The king is called the grandson of Kīrtivarma-Mahārāja, and the son of Vishṇuvardhana-Mahārāja, i.e., Kubja-Vishṇuvardhana.
ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/3 (page 9)
Placement
The Revenue Divisional Officer, Ellore, Kistna district.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Sarvalōkāśraya Śrī Vishṇu-vardhana-Mahārāja alias Rājarājadēva.
Date
2nd year
Language
Sanskrit in Telugu characters
Origin
Purchased for the Madras Government Museum.
Edition
…
Remarks
Registers the gift of the governorship (manni-ya-nibaddham-ādhipatyam) over 1,000 villages in Vēṅgīpura-vishaya to the chief Mummaḍi Bhīma of the Solar race, who was a much favoured subordinate of the king. The king is said to have been crowned in Tulā-lagna on Wednesday, the tenth day of the dark fortnight of Karka-ṭaka (Kuḷīra).
ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/4 (page 9)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Karkala, through the Collector of South Kanara.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1465, Śō-bhakṛit, ?? Chaitra, śu., 4, Friday.
Language
Kanarese
Origin
Returned to the Collector of South Kanara.
Edition
…
Remarks
Registers an agreement given to Keravasi Pāṇḍyapparasa by Tirumalarasa Chauṭaru, by which both the parties pledged them-selves to permanent alliance to help each other against enemies and not to entertain traitors from the other's camp. The witness to the transaction was Nāḍubaḷi Māramma-Heggaḍe.
ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/5 (page 9)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Do.
Language
Kanarese
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Records a similar agreement given by Pāṇḍyap-parasa, son of Chandaladēvī to Tiru-malarasa Chauṭaru. This is evidently the undertaking reciprocal to the above. The (Jaina) spiritual teacher Lalitakīrti-Bhaṭāra is mentioned.
ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/6 (page 9)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1450, Sarvadhāri, Vṛishabha, 14, Monday.
Language
Kanarese
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
This is an agreement given to the Chavuṭa chief of Tuḷuva and Nāḷina Tirumalarasa by Tirumalarasa Kinnika-Heggaḍe and Nāḷina Kinnika-Nimittaru entering into an alliance both offensive and defensive. The transaction was made in the presence of Śrīmat Kṛishṇānanda-Oḍeya.
ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/7 (page 10)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Karkala, through the Collector of South Kanara.

Remarks
This is a reciprocal copy of the above agree-ment, given by the Chavuṭa chief of Tuḷuva and Nāḷina Tirumalarasa to Kinnika-Heggaḍe Tirumalarasa and Nāḷina Kinnika-Nimittaru.
ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/8 (page 10)
Placement
The Patel of Kap, through the Stationary Deputy Tahsildar, Udipi, South Kanara district.
Dynasty
Vijayana-gara.
King
Virapratāpa Sadāśivarāya
Date
Śaka 1479, Naḷa, Kār-tika, śu., 1, Sunday.
Language
Sanskrit & Kanarese
Origin
Returned to the Deputy Tahsil-dar.
Edition
…
Remarks
Records the grant of some lands in the village Mai[lā]ra made by Tirumalarasa alias Madda-Heggaḍe, the chief of Kāp and his subordinate (?) Gaṇapaṇa-Sāmanta with the co-operation of the people of Kāp, at the instance of Dēvachandradēva for the spiritual benefit of his guru Munichandra-dēva.
ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/9 (page 10)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Uddi Nrisimha-charya of Kandukur, Mada-napalle taluk, Chittoor district, through the Kana-rese Assistant Mr. N.Laksh-minarayana Rao, M.A.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrapratāpa Veṅkaṭapatidēva-rāya.
Date
Śaka 1535, Pra-mādīcha, Vaiśākha, Śukla, dvā-daśī.
Language
Sanskrit in Nandi-Nāgari
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Registers a gift of lands made by the king to meet the expenses connected with certain festivals of the god Veṅkaṭanātha on the Phaṇigiri hill, i.e., Śēshāchala (viz., Tiru-malai).
ARIE/1921-1922/A/1921-22/10 (page 10)
Placement
M.R.Ry. R.Hari Rao, Kumbhakonam, through the Assistant Archaeological Superintendent for Epi-graphy.
Dynasty
Tanjore Nāyaka.
King
Vijayarāghava
Date
Śaka 1578 (ex-pired) Man-matha, Mīna, Śukla, Paur-namāsyā, Friday.
Language
Sanskrit in Telugu
Origin
Deposited in the Madras Mu-seum.
Edition
By Mr. G. Venkoba Rao in Ep. Ind.
Remarks
Registers the gift of a village called Alamēlu-maṅgāpuram as agrahāra to Vaishṇava brahmans who were learned in the Vēdas.

B.--Stone inscriptions copied in 1921 (continued from the last Annual Report).


ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/199 (page 11)
Placement
On the south wall of the central shrine in the Kāṅgēśvara temple at Kangayanallur.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Rājarājadēva
Date
41st year, Puraṭṭāśi
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers a gift of 10 paṇam received by Āṟṟuḻāṉ-[Taṉai] āḷum-Piḷḷai for burning a twilight lamp in the temple.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/200 (page 11)
Placement
On the east wall of the same shrine.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers that the (images of the) goddess for the sleeping hall (paḷḷi-aṟai) and of Kshētrapāla-Piḷḷaiyār in the temple of Ammaiappīśvaram-uḍaiya-Nāyaṉār are the gifts of one Aṇaippāḍi-Uḍaiyāṉ Pālaṉ.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/201 (page 11)
Placement
On the north and south walls of the same shrine.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1258, Dhātu, 15.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Fragment and stones misplaced. Seems to register a gift of land exempt from a number of taxes amongst which was Vaḷḷāḷadēvaṉvari. Mentions Kāṭṭuppāḍi.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/202 (page 11)
Placement
On the north wall of the Sundara-varadarāja Perumāḷ temple in the same village.
Dynasty
…
King
Sakalalōkachakravartin Śambuvarāya, ‘who took the earth by conquest.’
Date
17th year, Pramādi, Ṛishabha, śu, prathamā, Mon-day, Rōhiṇī.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers a sale of land for 170 Vīrachampaṉ-guḷigai by Kottambākkamuḍaiyāṉ Tiruvēṅgaḍamuḍaiyāṉ to the assembly (mahājana) of Śrī Mallinātha-chaturvēdimaṅ-galam and that of Kāṅgayanallūr alias Nīlakaṇṭha-chaturvēdimaṅgalam, a brahman village in Āndi nāḍu of Karaivaḻi.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/203 (page 11)
Placement
On the south wall of the Nāgēśvara temple at Serkad.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
[Ka]mpaṇa-Uḍaiyar
Date
Śaka 128[3 Śubha-kṛit], Tai, 8.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers the free colonization of the maḍaiviḷāgam by people, the taxes accruing there on being utilized for wor-ship in and repairs to the temple of Tirunāgīśvaram-uḍaya-Nāyaṉār at Śērkāḍu in Vaḷḷimalai-paṟṟu in Tuyil-nāḍu, a subdivision of Paḍuvūr-kōṭṭam, at the instance of the mahāpradhāni Sōmappa-Uḍaiyar, for the continuity of the rule of Kampaṇa-Uḍaiyar. Aḍaippam Nāgappa had the record engraved on stone.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/204 (page 11)
Placement
On a slab set up at the entrance of the same temple.
Dynasty

Do.

Śubhakṛit, Tai, 8
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Refers to the same transaction and to a sale, in lump sum, of the taxes levied in the Sōmappuḍaiya-maḍaiviḷāgam by the trustees of the temple.

Raudri

ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/208 (page 11)
Placement
On the north wall of the central shrine in the Bilvanāthēśvara temple at Tiruvallam.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Rājakēsarivarman, [‘who destroyed the ships at Kāndaḷūr-śālai’].
Date
13th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers that Araśūruḍaiyāṉ Īrāyiravaṉ Pallavayaṉ alias Mummuḍi-śōḻa Pōśaṉ, the supervisor of the temple of Tiruttīkkāli-Āḻvār at Tīkkāli-Vallam, in Mīyāṟu-nāḍu, a sub-division of Paḍuvūr-kōṭṭam, finding that one of the directors (gaṇattār) of the village had received 25 poṉ, weighed by the standard weight Dharmakaṭṭaḷai-tuḷai-niṟai, for burning a perpetual lamp founded by Śiṅga-pirāṭṭiyār and that his nephew or son-in-law (marumakaL) Śarvaḍichchaḍaṅgavi had neglected to maintain the lamp, now made a gift of 600 kuḻi of his land for continu-ing the charity.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/209 (page 12)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Rājakēsarivarman, ‘who destroyed the ships at Kāndaḷūr-śālai’.
Date
13th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers a gift of six ma of land, free of taxes, by the assembly of Tiruvallam to the same temple, in the regime of Araiśūruḍaiyāṉ Īrāyiravaṉ Pallavayaṉ alias Mummuḍi-śōḻa Pōśar for burning four lamps at the three sandhis of the day.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/210 (page 12)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Rājarajakēsarivarman, ‘who destroyed the ships at Śālai’.
Date
Do.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers the gift at the instance of the assembly of Tiru-vallam of certain ornaments to the same temple including one sacred string and pendant (tāli) (for the goddess) from the 40 kaḻañju and seven mañjāḍi of pure gold that had accumulated in the treasury from different sources. Mentions also the gift of a lamp and a jewelled ornament made by Mummuḍiśōḻa Pōśar.

ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/214 (page 12)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Uḍaiyār Rājēndra-dēva.
Date
Do.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Begins with the introduction tirumaruviya etc. which is much damaged. Registers a grant of land and of certain rights to the śivabrāhmaṇa, Gautamaṉ Rāmadēva-Bhaṭṭaṉ and his family for conducting the worship of the images of the god Śōḻakēraḷa-Viṭaṅkar alias Tribhuvana-sundara, his consort and the Piḷḷaiyār set up in the temple of Mahādēva of Tiruvallam by the assembly of Tiruvallam in Kaṟaivaḻi, a sub-division of Perumbāṇappāḍi in Jayaṅgoṇḍaśōḻa-maṇḍalam.

ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/216 (page 12)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.

Rājarājakēsarivarman, ‘who destroyed the ships at Kāndalūr-śālai.’
Date
13th year
Language
Tamil

Last portion of the inscription is built in. Registers a gift of 11 kaḻañju of gold to Tīkkāli-Āḻvār by Īrāyira-Pallava-raiyaṉ alias Mummuḍiśōḻa-Pōśar of Araiśūr in Teṉkarai Pāmbuṇi-kūṟṟam, a sub-division of Śōḻa-Nāḍu for conducting the pavitrārōhaṇa festival.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/217 (page 13)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Uḍaiyār Rājēndra-dēva.
Date
6th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Begins with the introduction tirumakaL maruviya, etc. Registers a gift of 1,500 kuḻi of land, to be brought under cultivation after clearing the forest, as an archanābhōga for worshipping the goddess Durgā standing in the north-ern corner of the temple, to the śivabrāhmaṇa mentioned in No. 214 above by the dēvakaṉmis and the residents of ....ṉūr, a dēvadāna (village) of the god Tiruvallam-Uḍaiyār in Karaivaḻi Tūy-nāḍu, a sub-division of Perum-bāṇappāḍi, a district of Jayaṅgoṇḍaśōḻa-maṇḍalam. Mention is made of Taṇiyamalai.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/218 (page 13)
Placement
On the west wall of the same shrine.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Rājarājakēsarivarman
Date
7th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers the details of expenditure for 74 kaḻañju of gold levied as a fine from the śivabrāhmaṇas for misappro-priating the temple lands and the 7 kaḻañju and 5 mañjāḍi which Madhurāntakaṉ Gaṇḍarādittaṉār, who scrutinized the temple accounts, had added to make up the deficit.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/219 (page 13)
Placement
On the west and south walls of the same shrine.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Rājarāja Rājakēsarivarman alias Rājarā-jarājadēva.
Date
22nd year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Refers to an increase of the pañchavāra paddy that the assembly of Mandiram alias Jayamēru-śrikaraṇamaṅga-lam, a dēvadāna of Tūy-nāḍu agreed to pay to the dēvakaṉmis of the temple at Tiruttīkkāli-Vallam in Mīyāru-nāḍu, a sub-division of Paḍuvūr-kōṭṭam. Mentions Īrāyiravaṉ Pallavaṉ alias Mummuḍiśōḻa-Pōśar, the lord of Araiśūr and an officer belonging to the perundaṉam of Rājarājadēva.
ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/220 (page 13)
Placement
On the same walls
Dynasty
Do.
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Rājendra-Chōḷa-dēva.
Date
6th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks

Mentions Aimbūṇi alias Viḍēlviḍugu Vikramāditta-chaturvēdimaṅgalam in Mīyāṟu-nāḍu, a subdivision of Paḍuvūr-kōṭṭam, a district of Jayaṅgoṇḍa-śōḻa-maṇḍalam. At the end of the inscription are en-graved certain further gifts of gold made in the 26th and 24th years of Rājādhirājadēva.

ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/222 (page 13)

On the same wall
Dynasty
Do.

Uḍaiyār Rājēndra-Chōḷadēva
Date
26th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Refers to the gift of gold for the sacred-string (tāli) and the ear-ornaments (mudrāvatāram) by the officer, Māndaikiḻār Māṟatamaṉ Nilaiyār alias Nittavinōda-Mūvēndavēḷār to the image of the consort of Paṉmāhēśvara-Viṭaṅkar set up by him, and to the gift of land to the image of Pāśupata-mūrti for śrībali and for offerings. Mentions the Kuḍiñjai-kkal equal in fineness to the Madurānta[ka]dēvaṉ-māḍai.

ARIE/1921-1922/B/1921/226 (page 14)
Placement

Parakēsarivarman alias Rājēndra-Chōḷa-dēva.

Records that certain dēvadāna lands of Takkōlam were pur-chased from the trustees of the temple of Tiruvūṟal-uḍaiya-Tambirāṉār at Vaḍa-Muḍigoṇḍaśōḻapuram alias Taṟkōlam in Pāśāli-nāḍu, a subdivision of Maṇavil-kōṭṭam, a district of Jayaṅgoṇḍaśōḻa-maṇḍalam who possessed these lands for conducting worship, for 100 poṉ by certain Paṇṭa Reḍḍis of Puṉṉaivayal in Paṉmā-nāḍu, a subdivision of the same kōṭṭam, for contribution towards the construction of the gōpura. From the interest accruing upon this sum the trustees had to provide an offering of curd-rice in the mornings.

Remarks
States that in pursuance of the royal order communicated to the Śiva and Vishṇu temples of Kāñchīpuram, Tirukkāḷatti, Tiruvoṟṟiyūr, Tiruvālaṅgāḍu and Tiruppālaivaṉam and the tax-free villages of the various temples in Chandragiri-rājya and in conformity with the orders of Ariyappa-Daṇṇāyaka Bhikshāvṛitti Aiyagaḷ and Dēvarāya-Uḍai-yar of Chandragiri, the Māhēśvaras and Vayirava-Nāyaṉār obtained an order to the effect that all the taxes and obligations except vibhūti-kāṇikkai which were due to the king from the temple of Tiruvūṟal-uḍaiya-Nāyaṉār must be deposited in the temple treasury and that out of this fund, worship, repairs and festivals had to be conducted in the temple by them.

Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vīrapratāpa Sadāśiva-Mahārāya, ‘who instituted the elephant hunt.’
Date
Śaka 1474, Parīdāpi, Tulā, śu., dvādaśī, Saturday, Rēvatī.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records that Śūrappa-Nāyaka, son of Pottappa-Nāyaka, who bears the title ‘Maṇināgapuravarādhīśvara,’ and who belonged to the Kāśyapa gōtra, made a gift of wet and dry lands for offerings and festivals to the god Āḻvārgaḷ-Nāyiṉār at Tirukkōvalūr on the southern bank of the Peṇṇai in Tiruvadi-śīrmai, a subdivision of Tirumuṉaippāḍi-vaḷanāḍu, which was itself a portion of Vaḻudiḷampaṭṭu-uśāvaḍi (i.e. chāvaḍi) in Kuṟukkai-kūṟṟam, a district of Malāḍu alias Jananātha-vaḷanāḍu. It is also recorded that a number of villages and lands which already belonged to the temple and had been assessed were lying uncultivated and that they were now made tax-free by Emberumāṉār-Jīyar. Services named after Aḷiya-Rāmarāyar. Śūrappa-Nāyakar and Kṛishṇama-Nāyākar are also referred to. Tirukkōvalūr is called the sacred place of the first three Āḻvārs (mudalāḻvār).

Date
Śaka 1427, Krō-dhana, Kumbha, śu., dvādaśī, Thursday, Puṇar-pūśam.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers that certain lands in the three banks out of twelve banks in the village (Tirukkōvalūr) were sold at a loss to the temple of Tiruviḍaikaḻi Nāyaṉār by the tenants owing to their inability to pay the taxes and that when Immaḍi Narasā-Nāyaka visited the temple on a dvādaśī day he made these lands tax-free, and ordered the profits thereon to be utilized for offerings and worship to the god on certain days every month. Immaḍi Narasayya-dēva and Vīramarasayya-Pallavaraiyaṉ are mentioned as the king's secretaries to whom the above oral orders were given.

Remarks
Records that as the taxes Iṉavari and Iḍaṅgai-vari collected from the Valaṅgai and Iḍaṅgai communities were exorbitant and the villagers were distressed and migrated to other places and the country became depopu-lated, the king had sent an order to Nāgarasa-Uḍaiyar authorising him to cancel these taxes, and as Aṇṇappa-Uḍaiyar to whom this order was communicated for execu-tion engraved it only at certain odd places, a further petition was preferred to Nāgarasa-Uḍaiyar and this order was then caused to be engraved at Tiruveṇṇai-nallūr.

States that, as the village of Tiruvāmāttūr was lying deserted for a long time, the temple maṇḍapas and gōpuras were ruined and the irrigation tank had breached, the king made a gift of certain taxes and ordered that from this amount, the necessary repairs should be carried out and worship conducted in the temple, in the name of Narasiṅgarāja-Uḍaiyar. The order was issued by Avasaram Aṉṉamara-śar, agent of the king, to the trustees of the temple who managed the temple lands.

ARIE/1921-1922/C/1922/282 (page 80)
Placement
On a slab set up in a forest near Dodra. Nowrangpur taluk. Jey-pore State, Vizagapatam Agency.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language
Nāgarī
Remarks
Mutilated and damaged. Describes the heroism and good qualities of a certain Gōpāladēva who defeated the chiefs of Gōkarṇa, Karṇāṭa, etc., and attained to the position of a rāṇaka. Registers the gift of the two villages Pippala-uṇḍī and Komvu as gurudakshiṇā by Maṇḍalapati to Paṇḍitāchārya Rāṇaka Śrī Vāvanadēva. The grant was renewed later by the princesses Sugaladēvī, the daughter of Sahadēva and Pampādēvī, the daughter of Rāṇaka Śrī Māṇatuṅga, the lord of Maṇḍābhōga, and by their sons. Among the witnesses figures the queen Vigrabamahādēvī.
ARIE/1921-1922/C/1922/283 (page 80)
Placement
On a slab set up on the Poḍāgaḍa hill near Bhandariguda in the same taluk.
Dynasty
…
King
Son of King Bhavadatta
Date
12th year (in words), Mādhava (i.e., Vaiśākha), [seventh] day.
Language
Sanskrit in Archaic Telugu
Remarks
Damaged. Begins with a praise of God Hari. The king Bhavadatta is said to have belonged to the race of Nala. Registers the installation of god Hari at the foot of Poḍa and the foundation of a satra (feeding house) for Brahmans and Yatis (ascetics) and the provision made in the shape of bhūri-dakshiṇā.

ARIE/1921-1922/C/1922/288 (page 80)
Placement
On three pillars of the Lakshmēś-vara temple at Gujaratipeta, Chipurupalli taluk, Vizagapatam district.
Dynasty
…
King
Vīra Śrī Pratāpa Viśvambharadēva Mahā-rāja.
Date
Pramōda, Kakaḍa (Karkaṭaka) 22nd day, pañchamī.
Language
Oriya
Remarks
Mr. T.C.Rath states that the inscription records the terms of the treaty entered into between Ibrahim Kutb Shah and Pratāp Viśvambhara Dēv Mahārāja at the Chieacole Fort and settles the payments to be made for the two villages Naṅdigām and Nerasama of Banthalō-kōṭa-muṭha after deducting the customary allowances to the village officers. Provision is also made for the offerings to be made at the temple of Lakhēśvara.
ARIE/1921-1922/C/1922/289 (page 80)
Placement
On a pillar of the ruined Muktīś-vara temple outside the village of Suravaram, Gannavaram taluk, Kistna district.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1189, Kārtika, Jīvavāra, (Thurs-day).
Language
Sanskrit in Telugu & Telugu
Remarks
States that Bōyu Mallaya, son of Goṇṭūri Nāvaprabhu granted a lamp and some land to the god Chōḍēśvara of Goṇṭūru. Mentions that Mallaya the grandfather of Bōya-Mallaya, got the governorship Śāsana of the place Velicheḍla from Rāyēndra-Chōḍa.

Records the gift of a lamp by Nalla Bhīma, son of.... yāditya to the temple of Nāgadēvēśvara. The 25 cows that were given for the ghee required for the lamp were kept in the custody of a shepherd named Lakshmaṇa.
